<div id="review_2250297512" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2250297512" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2250297512?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2250297512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17142638665900694424"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>When I was in high school, I would sometimes walk over to my best friend's house and we would sit down and write, and then post, fanfiction. Completely off-the-wall AU fanfiction, of the variety that's often known derisively as "crackfics." It was terrible fanfiction and, yes, it's still up - or was, last time I checked. And no, I'm not going to tell you where it was posted or under what name, because it was <i>bad</i>, and I was fifteen when I</span>
  <span id="freeText17142638665900694424" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>When I was in high school, I would sometimes walk over to my best friend's house and we would sit down and write, and then post, fanfiction. Completely off-the-wall AU fanfiction, of the variety that's often known derisively as "crackfics." It was terrible fanfiction and, yes, it's still up - or was, last time I checked. And no, I'm not going to tell you where it was posted or under what name, because it was <i>bad</i>, and I was fifteen when I wrote it.<i> We </i>had a good time writing it, though - and I think part of the reason we (foolishly) thought it was so great was because we poured a lot of our friendship and humor into the fic, to the point that the experience of writing the fic was greater than the sum of the parts.<br><br><br><br>I feel like that's kind of what happened in MY LADY JANE. These three authors, who I imagine are probably friends, decided to sit down together and compose their own fic - only it wasn't Ranma 1/2 or Inuyasha fic that they were writing about, but history itself. They <i>sat </i>down and they wrote fanfiction about Lady Jane Grey, and decided that Jane shouldn't die, so they turned her tragic ending and short-lived rule into a "spirited" romance, and they decided that Edward wasn't frail and sickly, but being poisoned instead. And they decided that the war between the Catholics and the Protestants would be much better written as a war between the, well, not-shape-shifters and the shape-shifters. And they <i>also </i>decided that shape-shifter was too banal, so they'd call them "edians" with a weird "d." CONFUSED YET? I WAS, TOO.<br><br><br><br>This is Tudor history crackfic, only it doesn't really work for a number of reasons.<br><br><br><br>Number 1) The narrative is condescending AF. The authors have all these constant <i>asides </i>written in parenthesis, which are obviously supposed to come across as adorable and funny and cute, but instead come across as overly precious and hand-holdy. "DID YOU GET MY JOKE? DID YOU?" It's literally the narrative equivalent of a four-year-old child thrusting their macaroni art into your face.<br><br><br><br>Number 2) The premise is stupid. When I got to the first page, I was like, "WTF." And then I got five pages deeper, and I was like, "ARE YOU KIDDING ME?" And by the time I got to the end of the book I was like, "HOLY HECK, YOU WEREN'T KIDDING ME." MY LADY JANE aspires to be many things - it wants to be Monty Python (and even rips several lines from it, including "It's just a flesh wound" and "your mother was a hamster, and your father smelled of elderberries"); it wants to be Ladyhawke (or East of the Sun, West of the Moon); it wants to be The Princess Bride; and I think it wants to be Blackadder as well, with all that heavy winking about history, but it fails at all of these because it isn't funny enough to be like Monty Python, it isn't tragic or well-scripted enough to be Ladyhawke, it isn't as romantic or as clever as Princess Bride, and it <i>especially </i>is not as historically astute as Blackadder, which had inside jokes about history down to an art form. This book's jokes about history is to mention anachronisms like Jimi Hendrix or to cheekily suggest that Edward was the inventor of the hover hand (no, I'm not kidding) or that <i>Jane </i>was the inspiration for using "ferret" as a verb instead of just a noun (because, you know, she can turn into a ferret). WTF, book?<br><br><br><br>Number 3) The characters have no depth and their personalities and motivations can LITERALLY be summed up in a single word. Observe. Edward: "Sex." Gifford: "G." Jane: "Books." Gracie: "Scottish." Mary: "Evil." ALL of their interactions and jokes are based around these words. Edward wants to have sex before he dies, and then when he meets a girl, obsesses over her single-mindedly. Gifford hates his name and wants to be called "G." Jane likes books in that annoying way that's typical of heroines, in that it compensates for her utter lack of personality, and panders desperately to us, the readers, who also like books (and is tantamount to a giant neon "PLEASE LIKE HER" sign). Gracie is a Scottish shape-shifter who acts like Merida, and for some reason her being Scottish is a Big Deal. Mary, who I always kind of felt sorry for, is branded as the villain. Because apparently it's not enough that she's got a drink named "Bloody Mary" named after her; she's got to be the cardboard cut-out villain in this book populated with Patricia Wrede rejects. Why not rename her Evil Evilsson?<br><br><br><br>Number 4) The humor is so dumb and lame. For example, Gracie is a fox shifter and Edward thinks she's hot, so the authors make this terrible joke: <i>Yes, Gracie was a fox. No, really. She was. Literally. (We know. It's too good.)</i> (47%). Bad pun, which the authors then feel the need to explain, and <i>then </i>feel the need to congratulate themselves for. The entire narrative is like that, and I found it really grating. Maybe some people will find it charming, but I prefer subtlety to sledgehammers. And here's an example of Jane showing us how much she likes to book her books when she books her booky books:  <i>"Armies aren't very good about carrying libraries with them. I can't imagine why. We'd fight so much less if everyone would just sit down and read" </i>(79%). In case you didn't get it: BOOKS.<br><br><br><br>I bought this because it was on sale for $1.99 at the time and because most of my friends said that they loved it. They <i>loved </i>it. I don't get it (I REALLY DON'T GET IT OKAY), but whatever, I'm glad they enjoyed it (even if I'm now second-guessing all of their recommendations to me). When I wrote that crazy fic with my friends, we had a few(!) readers who would actually egg us on to write more. They even subscribed via their emails so they could get UPDATES(!!!) when we posted. Young me was shocked that we had so few readers to appreciate our brilliance. Older, wiser me is amazed that we had any at all. I'm sure these authors were really proud of their book, and they had a lot of fun writing it, and probably all patted each other on the back for a job well done. And hey, for every naysayer like me, there's like a thousand people who ate this up like it was an ice cream sundae with the works. SO CLEARLY, <i>something </i>here worked for <i>some </i>people. But if you're going into this thinking it's going to be like Monty Python or The Princess Bride like I did, it's not. At all.<br><br><br><br>P.S. F**K YOU, G. YOUR NAME'S NOT A LETTER, YOU ELITIST BUTTMUFFIN.<br><br><br><br>1 star</span>
  <a data-text-id="17142638665900694424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2342384495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4354857234268414198">okay but the title shoulda been my king Edward cause he was the highlight of this book for me. until he wasn't. but still!<br/><br/><b> buddyread with </b> <a> chandler 👑 </a> and <a> veronique 🌹 </a> <br/><br/>so initially I said I wanted a wild ride, I wanted to laugh a ton & I wanted to understand what was going on. <br/>check, check & check !!<br/>but like... it was still kinda lacking. <br/>anyways, onward to the good! the bad! & my messy review! <br/><br/><b> Edward </b> : a teenage king suffering from the Affliction, with only a year to live and the poor boy h</span>
  <span id="freeText4354857234268414198" style="display:none">okay but the title shoulda been my king Edward cause he was the highlight of this book for me. until he wasn't. but still!<br /><br /><b> buddyread with </b> <a> chandler 👑 </a> and <a> veronique 🌹 </a> <br /><br />so initially I said I wanted a wild ride, I wanted to laugh a ton &amp; I wanted to understand what was going on. <br />check, check &amp; check !!<br />but like... it was still kinda lacking. <br />anyways, onward to the good! the bad! &amp; my messy review! <br /><br /><b> Edward </b> : a teenage king suffering from the Affliction, with only a year to live and the poor boy hasn’t even had his first kiss. it’s a sad life for Edward, who decides; <br /><br /><i> Life is short. And then you die. </i> <br /><br />not gonna lie, from the looks of things, he was a horrible king, but I STILL FELT BAD FOR MY BOY. like who to trust when everyone’s against you? so glad he pulled through. yeah yeah he was anti-feminist but that’s to be expected in that era, and he changed so it’s alllll good. <br /><br /><b> Jane </b> : so like, I think I expected to like her a lot more than I ended up liking her. she wasn’t exactly the most... intriguing? like i was kinda done with her bullshit near the end of the book. and like, I get she wasn’t expected to be reading YA fantasy but her obsession with books about literally everything wasn’t exactly relatable. but like. <br />she treats her books well. <br />that’s always nice. <br /><br /><b> Gifford </b> : when I say I love horses... I mean all horses except for Edians. kinda ruined the vibe for me, didn’t you G? and to think that he was actually ok with the nickname G? like noooope your Gifford Dudley in my book still, son. Needless to say; I didn’t really like him all that much. <br /><br /><b> BESS </b> : YOU SEE THAT ALL CAPS? it’s cause I actually loved her and needed more from her! Queen ELIZABETH?? my lack of history knowledge made that a plot twist folks, and I loved it. Like I literally. Wish. There. Was. More. Bess. She just seemed so smart &amp; fit to be queen. <br /><br /><b> Gracie </b> : yeah, nope. I’m done with “I can’t forget you’re king therefore I shan't accept your love for me” trope because like, the boy is in front of you in peasant clothes and he could be executed any minute I do not believe this counts as being "king". <br /><br />I did like the narration a lot though! I could hear the British voice going through my head as I read , and it added a load to the experience. <br /><br />In the end... I was just lacking some, like, realistic aspects? and somehow things always worked out in the favor of our trio. I thought there was going to be some excitement, especially when they were fighting the mythical bear but... nope. The fantasy was just stupid to be honest. <br /><br />Also... I’m no history person, I took the required credit in grade 10 and that’s about it, so I can’t say much about the accuracy. But technically speaking, it’s not supposed to be that accurate, right? so why y'all complaining?<br /><br />This did make me laugh though. You really have to read it for yourself, but it’s super light and entertaining. Like don’t expect executions and gory history and crazy fantasy - read this book when you’re ready to have some fun, relax, and read about (mostly Edward) but Lady Jane :) <br /><br />Now I actually have an interest in her beheading and I’m going to do some research !! <br />---------------------<br />INITIAL THOUGHTS ; <br />I’m diving headfirst into a book that supposedly will <br /> - make me laugh<br /> - give me a roller coaster ride <br /> - I don’t understand anything in the synopsis so I better understand what’s going on <br /> - I literally thought “Cynthia Hand” was “Claudia Gray” so yeah that’s me for you</span>

<div id="review_1799476123" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1799476123" />
    <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink"><img alt="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568991289p2/50044222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1799476123?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1799476123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12738715190342718220">Well this was an absolute delight.<br/><br/>All the hype was true! I was a bit worried at first but even at the introduction, I got it. I have to be honest though- I think this is the type of book that will really only appeal to you if this is your type of humor (very much British humor with nods to "Monty Python and the Holy Grail" and even little references to "The Princess Bride" and "Tangled" - yep, the Disney movie.)<br/><br/>Not to mention, the story was absolutely charming. Granted, I wasn't 100% familiar wi</span>
  <span id="freeText12738715190342718220" style="display:none">Well this was an absolute delight.<br /><br />All the hype was true! I was a bit worried at first but even at the introduction, I got it. I have to be honest though- I think this is the type of book that will really only appeal to you if this is your type of humor (very much British humor with nods to "Monty Python and the Holy Grail" and even little references to "The Princess Bride" and "Tangled" - yep, the Disney movie.)<br /><br />Not to mention, the story was absolutely charming. Granted, I wasn't 100% familiar with the real story- but I feel like I am now, even though this stretched the truth by miles (literally... and with humans having the magical ability to turn into animals.) The narrators frequently interject the story providing hilarious tid bits of information on actual history. Even still, it was a super light read and the perfect book if you're in the mood for comedic relief mixed in with a fantasy take on historical fiction. <br /><br />Really, the dedication says it all...<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Dedication<br /><br />For everyone who knows there was enough room for Leonardo DiCaprio on that door.<br /><br />And for England. We’re really sorry for what we’re about to do to your history.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />It follows 3 characters - Jane, Gifford, and Edward - who all have their fun little personalities. I was entertained on every page. Needless to say, though this might have been a little predictable at times- I was still hyped up and rooting for all of them individually. I have to say, Gifford was probably my favorite. His personality was hysterical and he was so precious - though Edward was right behind him.<br />Even with all the humor, some of the legit quotes in here surprised me..<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"The fool thinks he is wise," G retorted. "But the wise man knows himself to be a fool.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />Overall, this gets a standing ovation from me and a glowing recommendation- so long as you are clear on what to expect! Basically what I'm saying is this book is precious and needs to be a movie. <br /><br />Lastly, if you're looking for something similar- check out "These Vicious Masks"! This really reminded me of the humor in that book - both are a fun take on historical fiction with the added bonus of magic and comedic relief. <br /> <br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>

  <span id="freeText8722926802551592927" style="display:none"><b>4.75 stars!!!</b><br><br>Full mini review<br><br>I'm willing to <b>MARRY</b> a <b>horse</b> if it goes by the name of <b>Gifford Dudley</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517984218ra/25017306.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now this book is about the Tudors which were quite known as England's most notorious dynasty. What I love about this book is its captivating writing style and the charming characters. It was a delightful, exciting, magical, and hilarious book. <br><br>When I read this book, I became curious on what really happened to lady Jane Grey's reign for nine freaking days! I was also intrigued about her life and her adorable husband's life. I read the true story and I was amazed because the authors managed to recreate the history. They added humor, magic, adventure, and romance which made this book absolutely phenomenal. The authors combined their genius minds and impressive writing skills to come up with a bloody brilliant book.<br><br>Let's talk about Lady Jane. I like her character because she's headstrong, stubborn, smart, and of course, she's a bookworm. But what really made me fall in love with this book is Gifford Dudley or "G" for short. He's a gentleman. He's also smart, kind, charming, and funny. <br><br>I also liked this book because the two main characters were kind of falls to the category of "enemies to lovers". Their romantic relationship developed slowly. It was such a tease in a really good way.<br><br>All in all, this book was romantic, sweet, touching, witty, enchanting, and really incredible. I wasn't expecting to love this book. It surprised the hell out of me. I really can't wait to read the next book.</span>

<div id="review_1664978833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1664978833" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1664978833?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=days-of-old-aka-historical-fiction">days-of-old-aka-historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1664978833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13035434727932713993"><b>3 Stars</b> <br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>"My Lady, please! I am indecent."<br/>"You are,"Jane agreed. "Not to mention the fact that you are also unclothed.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>I'm not sure what I expected, but it definitely wasn't an alternate version of history where <b>Lady Jane Grey marries a were-horse.</b> <br/><br/>This takes a ton of fun tropes and mixes them together-- using 16th Century England as a starting point. As such, our story beings with Jane Grey's marriage and ascension to the throne. Instead of the Catholic/Protestant debacle this focuses on ma</span>
  <span id="freeText13035434727932713993" style="display:none"><b>3 Stars</b> <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"My Lady, please! I am indecent."<br />"You are,"Jane agreed. "Not to mention the fact that you are also unclothed.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I'm not sure what I expected, but it definitely wasn't an alternate version of history where <b>Lady Jane Grey marries a were-horse.</b> <br /><br />This takes a ton of fun tropes and mixes them together-- using 16th Century England as a starting point. As such, our story beings with Jane Grey's marriage and ascension to the throne. Instead of the Catholic/Protestant debacle this focuses on magic users vs non-magic users. <b>Only the magic is the ability to transform into a particular animal.</b><br /><br />...which ended up being my biggest problem with the book. While fun, the whole idea was incredibly silly. And it never sits well with me <b>when books have to <i>invent</i> some sort of oppression</b> for the heroes to struggle against. Especially when there was an actual real-life struggle that took place?? They had to invent a way for the privileged royalty to experience what marginalized groups faced every day for hundreds of years.<br /><br />But this just <b>isn't something you can take seriously.</b> There may be an entire rigged system, but this story is certainly not trying to discuss actual oppression. It's just an easy way to establish conflict so our heroes can take off on their journeys. <br /><br />From there <b>this was cute and silly.</b> It's definitely hard not to smile at all the Monty Python, Tangled and Princess Bride references. While none of the characters have much depth, they are still easy to root for and rather cute. It's not particularly original, but the narrative feels aware of the tropes which makes it feel like <b>the audience is included in a joke.</b><br /><br /><b>Overall</b><br />There's a few points that attempt to be serious, but overall this story is just for laughs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13035434727932713993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17317799284387884052">UPDATE 12-13-15<br/>The ARCs are here! Please ask the publicity department at HarperTeen, as we do not have very many ourselves to give away! So pretty!<br/><br/>UPDATE 10-15-15<br/>And WE HAVE A COVER, people. And it is oh-so-beautiful.<br/><br/>UPDATE 9-3-15<br/><br/>Well, the book is through copy edits, it has a cover (check back for the reveal), a jacket copy, and it is well under way to becoming a real book!<br/><br/>It turned out SO GREAT, you guys. It may be the best book, in some respects, that I have ever worked on. <br/><br/>Woohoo!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1457075209" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1457075209" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1457075209?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=laughed-my-pants-off">laughed-my-pants-off</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=swoon-worthy-hero">swoon-worthy-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=3rd-pov">3rd-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=alternative-history">alternative-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=excellent-writing">excellent-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=this-girl-is-awesome">this-girl-is-awesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1457075209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3059962182508861536"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"For everyone who knows there was enough room for Leonardo DiCaprio on that door.<br/>And for England. We’re really sorry for what we’re about to do to your history.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>So I was sitting here for a while thinking how to describe <i>My Lady Jane's</i> plot with words so you could get the main idea without spoiling anything. I did not find the right solution. Well, I could've given you quite a good summery, or even the one that GR has is okay, but my ultimate goal is to make you <i>want</i> to read this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText3059962182508861536" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"For everyone who knows there was enough room for Leonardo DiCaprio on that door.<br>And for England. We’re really sorry for what we’re about to do to your history.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>So I was sitting here for a while thinking how to describe <i>My Lady Jane's</i> plot with words so you could get the main idea without spoiling anything. I did not find the right solution. Well, I could've given you quite a good summery, or even the one that GR has is okay, but my ultimate goal is to make you <i>want</i> to read this book so much, you'll have no choice but to go grab a copy of it and start right away. After thinking (my brain still hurts) I decided to not overthink (huh, it's a little bit late for that?) and propose you to read a summery the authors have written for this book. Seriously, they've done all the work and I don't get why book sites don't put their annotation on the book's page? Now, <b>the reading of the summary below is strictly mandatory</b>; everyone who will refuse to read it will be hunted and burned at stake (with hay and torches and stuff (have to google what they used for pyres back in the 16th century). <br><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466976155i/19537056.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>Now, stop babbling, Nastassja, and get to action already!<br></p><p><b>The authors' summary (it's actually the book's prologue, but I am sure it can be used as a summery):</b><br><i><blockquote>You may think you know the story. It goes like this: once upon a time, there was a sixteen-year-old girl named Jane Grey, who was forced to marry a complete stranger (Lord Guildford or Gilford or Gifford-something-or-other), and shortly thereafter found herself ruler of a country. She was queen for nine days. Then she quite literally lost her head.<br>Yes, it’s a tragedy, if you consider the disengagement of one’s head from one’s body tragic. (We are merely narrators, and would hate to make assumptions as to what the reader would find tragic.)<br>We have a different tale to tell.<br>Pay attention. We’ve tweaked minor details. We’ve completely rearranged major details. Some names have been changed to protect the innocent (or not-so-innocent, or simply because we thought a name was terrible and we liked another name better). And we’ve added a touch of magic to keep things interesting. So really anything could happen.<br>This is how we think Jane’s story should have gone.<br>It begins in England (or an alternate version of England, since we’re dealing with the manipulation of history), in the middle of the sixteenth century. It was an uneasy time, especially if you were an E∂ian (pronounced eth-ee-uhn for those of you unfamiliar with the term). The E∂ians were blessed (or cursed, depending on your point of view) with the ability to switch between a human form and an animal one. For instance, certain members of the general public could turn themselves into cats, which greatly increased the country’s tuna-fish consumption, but also cut down on England’s rat population. (Then again, other individuals could turn into rats, so nobody really noticed.)<br>There were those who thought that this animal magic was terrific, but others who saw it as an abomination that needed to be eradicated immediately. That second group (known as Verities) believed that human beings had no business being anything other than human beings. And because Verities were largely in charge of everything, E∂ians were persecuted and hunted until most of them died out or went deep into hiding.<br>Which brings us to one fateful afternoon in the royal court of England, when King Henry VIII, during a fit of rage, transformed into a great lion and devoured the court jester, much to the audience’s delight. They clapped enthusiastically, for no one really liked the jester. (Later, the courtiers discovered the incident was not a rehearsed act of artful deception, but indeed an actual lion masticating the jester. When the audience found out the truth they no longer clapped, but they did remark, “That clown had it coming.”)<br>That very night, King Henry, once he’d returned to his human form, decreed that E∂ians weren’t so bad after all, and henceforth should enjoy the same rights and privileges as Verities. The decision to sanction the ancient magic made waves across Europe. The head of the Verity Church was not pleased with King Henry’s decision, but every time Rome sent a missive denouncing the decree, the Lion King ate the messenger.<br>Hence the phrase, Don’t eat the messenger.<br>When Henry died, his only son, Edward, inherited the throne. Our story begins in the middle of tense times, with an increasing animosity brewing between E∂ians and Verities, a teenage king with a tenuous grasp on the throne of England, and a young lord and lady who have no idea their destinies are about to collide.<br>Totally against their will.</blockquote></i><br>Finally, you know what the story is about and we can talk business. As you have probably noticed by the summery, this book is going to be <b>hilarious</b>. Every page of the story is filled with humor and irony, which do not border on vulgarity or toilet humor. You want an intelligent humor? You got it! It's the best treat this book has, and, honestly, it's not often I encounter funny books in YA (I can really count such books on my two hands), and, sadly, not every book can portrait real history (with minor changes, or course) and events that weren't so funny, after all, in an ironic way that makes us look at it under a different angle. <b>I can only applaud to the authors and how magnificently they expressed their collected voice in this book.</b><br><i><blockquote>“My lord, I will leave you to properly attire yourself. A carriage is waiting to take us to our honeymoon.” (The word honeymoon was quite new at this point in history, and actually involved a month’s supply of mead for the newlyweds rather than a romantic getaway, but for the sake of delicate sensibilities, we’ll pretend honeymoon meant then what it does now.)</blockquote>
<br><blockquote>Pet was on the other side, snarling and biting at those who would follow (gosh, we love that dog)</blockquote>
<br><blockquote>(Okay, so we told you that anybody could die at any time, and you seem like you’re getting worried, but Pet’s fine. &lt;...&gt; Trust us: we’re not the type of narrators who would kill a dog.)</blockquote>
<br><blockquote>They collapsed into each other, and although it would be indelicate to detail what happened next, these narrators will tell you that a “very special hug” does not begin to describe it.<br>P.S. They totally consummated.</blockquote></i><br>Look, how smartly they inserted remarks and clarification on certain events and words that after a while you wait for such remarks to appear and clarify something else for you, because it's simply fun, and you like authors' voice so much, you want more of it: it creates the illusion of watching a play in the theater.<br></p><p>Aside from the awesome approach with the history material, this book gave us wonderful characters, which according to history books (you won't find those anywhere in public places, because they are highly encrypted and kept in a far far away lands... but I give you my word: they contain only the truth) invented such things as using a pan to bash someone's head (yup, Disney Rapunzel wasn't the first to think of such useful thing) and invented an arm-stretch move on a young woman and ect. and ect. (I will need hours to count all inventions, really). Such a creative creatures these characters. Here's the cast:<br></p><p>
  <i> a horse</i>
  <br>
</p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/371214.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>
  <i>a kestrel</i>
  <br>
</p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466976155ra/19537057.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>
  <i>a ferret</i>
  <br>
</p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466976155ra/19537058.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>
  <i>a fox</i>
  <br>
</p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466976155ra/19537059.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>
  <i>a skunk</i>
  <br>
</p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466976155ra/19537060.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>I know, I know, I can guess what you are about to say, "What the... animal planet you are showing us?!" But it is the real cast of this book, though I can't tell you who is who: you'll have to read the book to find out. But for one character I can make a disclosure, because his special condition is mentioned in the first chapter, so you will not have to wait long to meet him (look at the beautiful chestnut horse on the first picture). <i>G</i> (his name is <i>Gifford</i> but he - by the obvious reasons - prefers to be called G) has an <i>equestrian situation</i> and literary turns into horse from every sunrise till every sunset. With the perks of being a horse other things apply, such as eating hay (but he prefers apples, really), um, manure and horse rules such as: do not ride the horse, do not tell horse jokes, do not bridle the horse... agh, too many rules for one horse, don't you think? Not an easy life I can assure you. As for our other characters (and we have three main characters as you already guessed: one for every author from our lovely team of ladies), they too have a couple of surprises to show you (and they can't wait for you to start the book) and a very exciting tale to tell.<br></p><p>So here's <b>my verdict</b>, folks: if you want a funny (a veryyyyy funny) story to read, and reliable headstrong characters to meet, and to learn the <i>real</i> version of English history - READREADREADREADREADREADREADREADREADREADREADREAD <i>My Lady Jane</i> (the pyre is still burning if you were wondering, no pressure here) and get your dose of fun that will stay with you for a long time after you finish and close the book. <br></p><p><b>P.S.</b> I couldn't leave you without mentioning that the heroine in whose honor this book is named - Jane - is a huge lover of books (she is also a 16 years-old spinster and a redhead and as you can imagine the combination is not a very good one for the 16th century England, but, hey, the girl does really know how to use a pan occasionally). Now I am really off to do... stuff <i>*curtsies and vanishes behind the curtain*</i></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="3059962182508861536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RuqDAhu8Q99+QUd4WHNmTCM4GgL2ZK9VZdHigTdacF0js5EsIxFhfdtUmoujQmB4h4YJExK5XO84c6hJsqn+ww==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9415884004968313986">Cynthia Hand is the New York Times bestselling author of several books for teens, including the UNEARTHLY trilogy, THE LAST TIME WE SAY GOODBYE, MY LADY JANE and MY PLAIN JANE (with fellow authors Brodi Ashton and Jodi Meadows), THE AFTERLIFE OF HOLLY CHASE, and the upcoming novels THE HOW AND THE WHY and MY CALAMITY JANE (also with Ashton and Meadows). Before turning to writing for young adults, </span>
  <span id="freeText9415884004968313986" style="display:none">Cynthia Hand is the New York Times bestselling author of several books for teens, including the UNEARTHLY trilogy, THE LAST TIME WE SAY GOODBYE, MY LADY JANE and MY PLAIN JANE (with fellow authors Brodi Ashton and Jodi Meadows), THE AFTERLIFE OF HOLLY CHASE, and the upcoming novels THE HOW AND THE WHY and MY CALAMITY JANE (also with Ashton and Meadows). Before turning to writing for young adults, she studied literary fiction and earned both an M.F.A. and a Ph.D. in fiction writing. She currently resides in Boise, Idaho, with her husband, two cats, one crazy dog, two kids, and mountain of books.</span>
